Refuting the Objection: Naming Oneself a Believer is Not Pride
Maturidi refutes the objection using analogy and prophetic example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the objection that calling oneself a believer is an act of pride by pointing to contradictions in the objector's stance regarding righteousness and piety.

Core Idea
Calling oneself a believer is not pride; it is like calling oneself righteous, which even prophets did.

This lesson addresses a common criticism: that declaring oneself a believer amounts to self-praise. Maturidi begins by presenting the objection and then dismantles it by drawing parallels with righteousness and piety, showing that if one cannot call themselves righteous, then they cannot call themselves believers either. He also invokes the example of prophets to show that fear does not negate faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying the objection
Read the Arabic passage once. Identify the objector's claim: that calling oneself a believer could be a lie and a major sin, and therefore amounts to pride.
Look for the phrase 'الكذب الذي لعله كبيرة'.
2
Notice the contradiction with righteousness
Maturidi points out that the objector's own argument applies equally to righteousness (بر) and piety (تقوى). If testifying to righteousness invites fear of wrath, then the same applies to faith.
Consider the verses Maturidi quotes about the righteous.
3
Reflect on the prophets' example
Maturidi cites that prophets supplicated with fear and hope, yet they were not afflicted with major sins. This shows that fear does not remove the name of faith.
How does this undermine the objector's claim that fear is incompatible with faith?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن المؤمن لا خوف عليه، لم لا تخافون من تسميتكم أنفسكم مؤمنين؟ الكذب الذي لعله كبيرة يزيل عنكم اسم الإيمان، فيكون التسمية من كبر أنفسكم، وقد حذرتم عن تزكية الأنفس بقوله تعالى: {فلا تزكوا أنفسكم} [النجم: 32]. ثم تعارضون بالبر والتقوى أتشهدون أنفسكم بهما أو لا؟ فإن شهدوا لزمهم بالخوف في المتقين الأبرار أن يكونوا استوجبوا مقت الله والخلود في النار فيكون جهنم دار المتقين الأبرار لا دار الفاسقين؛ وقد قال الله تعالى: {وإن الأبرار لفي نعيم} [الانفطار: 13] الآية، ويبطل الدعاء بقوله: {وتوفنا مع الأبرار} [آل عمران: 193]. وإن أبوا التسمية بذلك لزمهم مثله في الإيمان، إذ هو اسم لما مقت الله كالبر والتقوى. ثم يقال: إنه قد ثبت عن الأنبياء والرسل أنهم كانوا يدعون الله رغباً ورَهَبًا وخوفا وطمعاً ويزعمون أنهم لم يبتلوا بكبائر، فقد كان هذا الخوف ينل بها، لم لا دلكم أن ليس ترك بيان الحد لما يخاف ويرجى، بل ذلك لما الله معاقبة شاء بالصغائر؟ ومن قولكم إن ما يوجب العقوبة يزيل اسم الإيمان، فاعتبروا بأن لستم مؤمنين على ما أخبرتم في الحقيقة. والله الموفق.

وقد قال الله تعالى: {إنما المؤمنون الذين آمنوا بالله ورسوله ثم لم يرتابوا} [الحجرات: 15]. وعندكم المؤمن لا يخاف نقمة الله ولا يرجو رحمته بل قد استوجب رحمته لو كان مؤمنا، وليس الله أن يعذبه لو كان مؤمنا، والإيمان هو الذي حملهم على ذلك. فكيف ألزمتموهم الخوف وذلك ليس على المؤمن في الحقيقة ومنعتموهم على الارتياب في الإيمان، والارتياب فيه بما رأى الخوف؟ وذلك بين التناقض. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
That the believer has no fear upon him. Why do you not fear from naming yourselves believers? The lie that perhaps is a major sin removes from you the name of faith, so the naming is from the pride of your souls, and you have been warned against self-justification by His saying: 'Do not justify yourselves' [Q. 53:32]. Then you contradict with righteousness and piety: do you testify for yourselves with them or not? If they testify, then fear would be incumbent upon them concerning the pious righteous that they have deserved Allah's wrath and eternal abiding in the Fire, so Hell would be the abode of the pious righteous, not the abode of the wicked. And Allah has said: 'Indeed the righteous are in bliss' [Q. 82:13] the verse, and it invalidates the supplication by His saying: 'And cause us to die with the righteous' [Q. 3:193]. And if they refuse the naming by that, the like of it is incumbent upon them concerning faith, since it is a name for what Allah hates like righteousness and piety. Then it is said: It has been established from the prophets and messengers that they used to supplicate Allah with desire and awe, fear and hope, and they claim that they were not afflicted with major sins. Now this fear they attained it – why did it not indicate to you that the omission of explaining the limit is not for what is feared and hoped, but rather that is for what Allah punishes if He wills among minor sins? And from your saying that what necessitates punishment removes the name of faith, then consider that you are not believers according to what you have informed in reality. And Allah is the Grantor of success.

And Allah has said: 'Indeed the believers are those who have believed in Allah and His Messenger and then have not doubted' [Q. 49:15]. And according to you, the believer does not fear Allah's vengeance nor hope for His mercy, but rather he has merited His mercy if he were a believer, and Allah is not to punish him if he were a believer, and faith is what impelled them to that. So how have you made fear incumbent upon them, while that is not upon the believer in reality, and you prevented them from doubt in faith, and doubting in it because of the fear they saw? That is manifest contradiction. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. Maturidi begins by stating the objection: why are you not afraid of calling yourselves believers? The objector argues that calling oneself a believer could be a lie, which is a major sin that removes the name of faith, implying pride. Maturidi then points out a contradiction: if they claim righteousness and piety, they would have to fear deserving Allah's wrath, but the Quran promises bliss for the righteous. If they refuse to call themselves righteous, the same applies to calling themselves believers, since faith is also a name for what Allah loves. He then cites that prophets themselves supplicated with fear and hope, proving that fear does not negate faith. Finally, he contrasts their position with the Quranic description of believers as those who do not doubt, showing that their imposition of fear contradicts the nature of true faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
خوف
كبيرة
بر
تقوى
تزكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that declaring oneself a believer is an act of pride that nullifies faith.
Correction: Maturidi shows that calling oneself a believer is not pride but a declaration of hope and submission, as even prophets did.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the objection that calling oneself a believer involves pride fail?
A) Because the believer is secure and has no fear at all.
B) Because prophets also feared, yet they were believers.
C) Because calling oneself a believer is a lie that removes faith.
D) Because the Quran forbids self-justification absolutely.

Key Takeaway
Calling oneself a believer is not pride; it is like calling oneself righteous, which even prophets did, and fear does not negate faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call yourself a believer, do you sense any hidden pride in your heart? Maturidi challenges us to examine whether our declaration stems from hope and submission or from self-justification. Will you honestly assess your intention the next time you say 'I am a believer'?
?
The prophets supplicated with fear and hope despite their sinlessness. Have you been avoiding fear in your worship, thinking it shows weak faith? How can you this week intentionally combine both fear and hope in your du'a, as the prophets did?
?
You regularly pray 'Cause us to die with the righteous' (Q. 3:193) — but do you truly see yourself as one of them? If not, what holds you back? Maturidi's argument forces you to confront: if you refuse to call yourself righteous, consistency demands you also refuse to call yourself a believer. Are you ready to embrace the identity He has given you?

Prophets Feared Allah Yet Were Believers: A Contradiction Exposed
Maturidi uses Quranic verse to expose contradiction in objector's logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how Maturidi uses the Quranic description of believers as those without doubt to argue that fear does not negate faith, exposing a contradiction in the objector's position.

Core Idea
True believers are described as free from doubt, not free from fear—Maturidi exposes the flaw in equating fear with disbelief.

In this continuation, Maturidi quotes the Quran: 'The believers are those who have believed and then have not doubted.' He then shows that the objector's demand for fear contradicts this description. If believers are not supposed to doubt, then how can they be required to fear? This reveals an inconsistency in the argument against calling oneself a believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the new passage and identify the Quranic verse
Read the Arabic passage. Note the verse 'إِنَّمَا الْمُؤْمِنُونَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَرْتَابُوا' (Q. 49:15). Understand that the verse emphasizes certainty without doubt.
The word 'يرتابوا' means 'doubt'.
2
Understand Maturidi's logical argument
Maturidi argues that according to the objector's view, a believer would have no fear and no hope, but this contradicts the verse. The objector imposes fear on believers, yet the Quran says believers do not doubt. This is a contradiction.
Trace the logical steps: objector's premise → consequence → contradiction.
3
See how this refutes the objector
Maturidi concludes that the objector's position leads to a manifest contradiction. The true believer does not doubt, but the objector's requirement of fear creates doubt in faith.
Reflect on the final statement 'لا قوة إلا بالله' as a reminder of reliance on Allah.

Sin Under Duress and Divine Grace
Maturidi presents two arguments: sin under duress and divine grace.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that a believer sinning under emotional duress does not become a disbeliever, and how divine grace preserves the believer's enmity with Satan.

Core Idea
Emotional duress does not turn a believer into a disbeliever; Allah's grace distinguishes involuntary sin from worship.

This lesson explores two of Maturidi's arguments for why sins committed under overwhelming desire, anger, or zeal do not constitute disbelief. The third argument focuses on the believer's intention being like one driven, not one obedient to Satan. The fourth argument appeals to divine grace: Allah does not label such acts as worship because that would be too harsh. Both arguments preserve the believer's identity as a believer despite the sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for Maturidi's concise style. Then read the literal translation. Notice the two distinct arguments presented consecutively.
The Arabic begins with 'وأيضا' indicating an additional point.
2
Identify the two arguments
The passage contains two separate points: the third argument about being 'driven' (مدفوع) by desire, anger, or zeal, and the fourth argument about divine grace (فضل) not requiring such acts to be considered obedience to Satan.
The transition to the fourth argument is signaled by 'وأمكن أن يقال'.
3
Understand the concept of 'driven'
Maturidi says the believer is 'like one driven' (كالمدفوع) meaning he does not intend disobedience or obedience to Satan; rather, he is overcome. Therefore, disbelief does not follow, and God will reward him for the means of resistance He gave.
The term 'مدفوع' implies coercion, not free choice.
4
Reflect on divine grace
The fourth argument states that Allah, out of grace, does not label such sins as obedience to Satan or worship, because He knows the severity it would impose. Instead, He preserves the believer's enmity with Satan even during sin.
This grace honors the believer by not treating him as a worshipper of Satan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن كل مؤمن فيما يعصى الله في شيء يكون كالمدفوع إليه، بما يغلب عليه من شهوة أو غضب أو حمية أو نحو ذلك مما به يصير إليه. إذا لم يقصد عصيان الرب أو طاعة الشيطان بل يصير من الوجه الذي ذكرت كالمدفوع، فلم يلزم الكفر به، والله أن يجزيه عليه بما ملكه ما به يمتنع عن الدفع إليه. ولا قوة إلا بالله . وأمكن أن يقال: ذلك فضل الله إلى عباده أن لم يلزمهم بمثل ذلك طاعة الشيطان وعبادته ، إذ علم شدة ذلك عليهم ؛ على ما أكرمهم الله في حال العصيان بمعاداة الشيطان
And also, every believer, when he disobeys God in something, is like one driven to it, by what overwhelms him of desire or anger or zeal or the like of that which brings him to it. Since he does not intend disobedience to the Lord or obedience to Satan, but rather becomes, from the aspect you mentioned, like one driven, so disbelief does not necessarily follow from it, and God will reward him for it with what He has given him, by which he refrains from being driven to it. And there is no power except with Allah. And it may be said: That is Allah's grace to His servants, that He did not require them to consider that as obedience to Satan and worship of him, since He knew the severity of that upon them, just as He honored them, in the state of disobedience, with enmity toward Satan.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage contains Maturidi's third and fourth arguments. The third argues that a believer sinning under the duress of overwhelming desire, anger, or zeal is like one driven (madfu'), not intending to obey Satan, so disbelief does not follow. God will reward him according to the ability He gave to resist. The fourth argument appeals to divine grace: God does not label such acts as obedience to Satan because that would be too severe; instead, He preserves the believer's enmity with Satan even while sinning.

Key Terms
مدفوع (driven)
شهوة (desire)
غضب (anger)
فضل (grace)
عداوة (enmity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any sin committed under emotional compulsion automatically constitutes disbelief.
Correction: Maturidi argues that if the believer does not intend obedience to Satan but is driven by overwhelming desires or emotions, disbelief does not necessarily follow. Allah's grace further prevents labeling such acts as worship.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's third argument, why does the believer not become a disbeliever when sinning under the influence of desire?
A) Because the sin is not actually committed
B) Because he does not intend obedience to Satan
C) Because he repents immediately
D) Because the sin is minor

Key Takeaway
Maturidi teaches that sins committed under emotional duress do not negate faith, and Allah's grace ensures such acts are not counted as worship of Satan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you sinned because you were overwhelmed by anger or desire. Did you feel your faith was shattered? How does this lesson change the way you view your relationship with God in that moment? Will you now turn to His grace instead of despair?
?
You have likely judged yourself or others harshly for sins committed under strong emotion. This lesson says God knows the severity of that. Can you truly accept that God's grace covers such weakness? What do you need to release to really believe that?
?
In your life, what duress-driven habit do you believe God sees but you struggle to forgive yourself for? After reading this passage, what concrete step will you take to reconcile that act with your faith and keep enmity toward Satan?

The True Meaning of Obedience: Command, Not Pleasure
Maturidi defines obedience and refutes the notion that pleasing Satan constitutes obedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that obedience in Islamic theology is defined by acting upon a command, not by the resulting pleasure of the one being obeyed.

Core Idea
Obedience is defined by command, not by pleasure.

Maturidi begins his refutation of a claim by establishing a precise definition of obedience. He argues that simply pleasing Satan does not constitute obedience to him; rather, obedience requires intentional compliance with a command. This lesson unpacks that definition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of Maturidi's argument. Notice the logical flow from definition to application.
Pay special attention to the phrase 'الطاعة هي التي تُؤدَّى على الأمر'.
2
Identify the definition of obedience
Find the sentence that gives the definition of obedience. Write it down in Arabic and English.
3
Apply the definition to Satan
See how Maturidi uses the definition to argue that actions pleasing Satan are not necessarily obedience, because they are not done by his command.
He distinguishes between doing something because of command and doing it for other reasons (like personal desire).
4
Reflect on the supporting argument
Consider why Maturidi mentions that God cannot be described as obeying servants. How does this support the definition?
This shows that defining obedience by pleasure would lead to absurdity.
5
Conclude the lesson
Summarize: obedience requires a command; pleasure alone is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول في ذلك بوجوه. أحدها أن ليس في ذلك طاعةٌ للشيطان وإن كان هو يُسرّ به ويتلذذ لشؤم طبعه وسوء اختياره، إذ لم يكن الذي يتعاطاه يفعله لأمره ودعائه إليه، والطاعة هي التي تُؤدَّى على الأمر لا على ما يُسرّ ويتلذذ ؛ لأن للعباد، فيما أعطاهم الله الشهواتِ لذات وسرورا، ومحال وصف الله بالطاعة لهم، أو يمكن الأمر منهم إياه بالفعل. دل أن ليس ذلك الوجه هو سبيل معرفة الطاعة. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
والثاني أن الديانات من اعتقادات لا أفعال تكتسب، إذ الاعتقادات لا يجرى عليها القهر والغلب، ولا لأحد من الخلائق على اعتقادِ آخَرَ ومُنْعِه سلطان؛ وهن أفعال القلوب خاصة. وربما كان للألسن بها تعلّق من حيث لا يُقدر على استعمال لسانِ غيره وكذلك قلبه، ويُقدر على سائر الجوارح. وإذا كانت الديانات كما ذكرنا، والكفر والإيمان دين، لم يصر الذي ذكرت - لو كان طاعة ـ دينا . والكفر دين، فكيف وهو من الوجه الذي ذكرت ليس بطاعة. وقد روى عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه أجاب لهذا السؤال أن الذي ذكرته حق القصد لا حق الوقوع على حال لا يقصد ذلك. وعلى ذلك أمور علّقت بالقصد، وذلك يخرج على ما بينا من ترتيب الاعتقادات . ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then we say regarding that with aspects. One of them: there is no obedience to Satan in that, even if he is delighted and takes pleasure due to his evil nature and bad choice, because the one who does it does not do it by his command and invitation. Obedience is that which is performed upon command, not upon what delights and pleasures. Because servants, in what God has given them of desires, have pleasures and delights, and it is impossible to describe God as obeying them, or that they can command Him with an act. This indicates that this aspect is not the way of knowing obedience. There is no power except with God. The second: religions are beliefs, not acquired acts, because beliefs are not subject to coercion and overpowering, and no creature has authority over the belief of another or to prevent him; they are specifically acts of the hearts. Perhaps tongues have a connection to them insofar as one cannot use another's tongue nor his heart, but can with other limbs. Since religions are as we said, and disbelief and faith are a religion, then what you mentioned—if it were obedience—would not become a religion. Disbelief is a religion, so how [could it be] when from the aspect you mentioned it is not obedience. It has been narrated from Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, that he answered this question: what you mentioned is true in intent, not in actual occurrence in a case where one does not intend that. And upon that, matters are tied to intent, and that comes out according to what we explained of the ordering of beliefs. There is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage presents the first two arguments (الوجه الأول والثاني) in a series of refutations against the claim that certain actions constitute obedience to Satan or worship of him. The first argument defines obedience strictly as acting upon a command. The fact that Satan may be pleased by an action does not make it obedience, because the doer does not perform the act by Satan's command. Obedience is defined by the intention to follow a command, not by resulting pleasure. The second argument establishes that religions (including disbelief and faith) are matters of belief (اعتقادات), not acquired actions. Beliefs cannot be coerced; they are acts of the heart. Even if speech has some connection, one cannot control another's heart. Therefore, an action that might theoretically be considered obedience cannot transform into a religion, since religions are defined by beliefs. The passage also cites Abu Hanifa, who clarifies that the issue is about intentionality—actions are judged by intent.

Key Terms
طاعة
أمر
شيطان
لذة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any action that pleases Satan is obedience to him.
Correction: Obedience requires acting upon a command; pleasure alone does not constitute obedience.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, what is the defining characteristic of obedience?
A) The action brings pleasure to the one being obeyed.
B) The action is performed upon command.
C) The action is good in itself.
D) The action is performed frequently.

Key Takeaway
Obedience is defined by acting upon a command, not by the pleasure it brings to the one being obeyed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever justified a sin because it felt good or seemed harmless, forgetting that obedience to Allah requires His command, not your pleasure? What would it take for you to abandon that action today?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you ever check your intention: am I doing this because Allah commanded it, or because I enjoy the feeling? Be honest—if the pleasure were gone, would you still obey?
?
Consider a time you assumed someone's action was good simply because it pleased you. How might you have been wrong about what true obedience to Allah requires? Will you start measuring actions by the Qur'an and Sunnah instead of your own preferences?

Faith and Disbelief

Religion as Belief, Not Action
Maturidi defines religion as beliefs, argues they are not coercible, and concludes that disbelief cannot be obedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi defines religion (dīn) as beliefs (iʿtiqādāt) rather than acquired actions, and how this refutes the idea that disbelief could be considered obedience.

Core Idea
Religions are beliefs, not actions; coercion has no power over belief.

In his second argument, Maturidi establishes that religions—including faith and disbelief—are fundamentally matters of belief, not action. Beliefs cannot be coerced; they are acts of the heart. This distinction is crucial for understanding why certain actions cannot transform into religion. Maturidi also cites Abu Hanifa to emphasize the role of intention.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the second argument
Read the Arabic passage. Focus on the definition of religion and the reasoning that follows.
Notice the structure: claim, proof, inference, and a citation from Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the key claim about religions
Find where Maturidi says 'الديانات من اعتقادات لا أفعال تكتسب' and note it.
3
Understand why beliefs cannot be coerced
Read the explanation that beliefs are acts of the heart and not subject to overpowering. Contrast with actions of the limbs.
The passage says: 'الاعتقادات لا يجرى عليها القهر والغلب'.
4
Apply to the question of obedience
See how this leads to the conclusion that disbelief, being a religion, cannot be considered obedience if obedience is defined by command.
Also consider the Abu Hanifa quote about intent.
5
Reflect on the role of intention
Think about how the Abu Hanifa quote ties actions to intent, and how that relates to the overall argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول في ذلك بوجوه. أحدها أن ليس في ذلك طاعةٌ للشيطان وإن كان هو يُسرّ به ويتلذذ لشؤم طبعه وسوء اختياره، إذ لم يكن الذي يتعاطاه يفعله لأمره ودعائه إليه، والطاعة هي التي تُؤدَّى على الأمر لا على ما يُسرّ ويتلذذ ؛ لأن للعباد، فيما أعطاهم الله الشهواتِ لذات وسرورا، ومحال وصف الله بالطاعة لهم، أو يمكن الأمر منهم إياه بالفعل. دل أن ليس ذلك الوجه هو سبيل معرفة الطاعة. ولا قوة إلا بالله .

Then we say regarding that with aspects. One of them: there is no obedience to Satan in that, even if he is delighted and takes pleasure due to his evil nature and bad choice, because the one who does it does not do it by his command and invitation. Obedience is that which is performed upon command, not upon what delights and pleasures. Because servants, in what God has given them of desires, have pleasures and delights, and it is impossible to describe God as obeying them, or that they can command Him with an act. This indicates that this aspect is not the way of knowing obedience. There is no power except with God. The second: religions are beliefs, not acquired acts, because beliefs are not subject to coercion and overpowering, and no creature has authority over the belief of another or to prevent him; they are specifically acts of the hearts. Perhaps tongues have a connection to them insofar as one cannot use another's tongue nor his heart, but can with other limbs. Since religions are as we said, and disbelief and faith are a religion, then what you mentioned—if it were obedience—would not become a religion. Disbelief is a religion, so how [could it be] when from the aspect you mentioned it is not obedience. It has been narrated from Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, that he answered this question: what you mentioned is true in intent, not in actual occurrence in a case where one does not intend that. And upon that, matters are tied to intent, and that comes out according to what we explained of the ordering of beliefs. There is no power except with God.

Misconception: Religion is primarily about actions that can be coerced.
Correction: Religion is about beliefs (iʿtiqādāt), which are acts of the heart and cannot be coerced.

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, why can't religion be defined as acquired actions?
A) Because actions can be coerced.
B) Because beliefs are not subject to coercion.
C) Because actions are not important.
D) Because religion is only about faith.

Key Takeaway
Religions are defined by inner beliefs, not by external actions; beliefs are acts of the heart that cannot be coerced.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever tried to change someone's belief through argument or pressure? What does this passage reveal about your inability to truly control another's heart, and how does that humble your approach to sharing faith?
?
Consider a time when your outward actions did not align with your inner beliefs. What does Maturidi’s insistence that religion is about belief—not actions—say about the state of your heart? Are you satisfied with that disconnect?
?
Abu Hanifa ties matters to intent. When you perform acts of worship, is your heart genuinely present and intending closeness to God, or are you merely going through motions? What one change can you make today to bring your actions into harmony with your beliefs?

Believers’ Involuntary Sins and Divine Grace
Maturidi's third argument and explanation of divine grace regarding involuntary sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why involuntary sins do not constitute disbelief and how God's grace prevents them from being considered worship of Satan.

Core Idea
God does not label involuntary sins as worship of Satan.

Imam Maturidi presents a third argument addressing the difficult case of believers who sin under compulsion from desire or anger. He explains that such acts do not entail disbelief, and then reveals a profound divine grace: God withholds the name of obedience and worship from these sins, understanding human weakness. This lesson explores the argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two parts: the argument about compulsion, and the grace explanation.
Pay attention to the term 'مدفوع' (driven) in the first part.
2
Identify the key distinction
The passage distinguishes between intentional disobedience and being driven by desires. Understand why the former is not considered disbelief.
Look for the phrase 'إذا لم يقصد عصيان الرب' (when he does not intend to disobey the Lord).
3
Reflect on the two aspects of grace
The passage lists two ways God shows grace: withholding the name of worship, and giving hope of forgiveness. Consider how this encourages believers.
The second aspect is tied to the believer's enmity toward Satan even while sinning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن كل مؤمن فيما يعصى الله في شيء يكون كالمدفوع إليه، بما يغلب عليه من شهوة أو غضب أو حمية أو نحو ذلك مما به يصير إليه. إذا لم يقصد عصيان الرب أو طاعة الشيطان [بل] يصير من الوجه الذي ذكرت كالمدفوع، فلم يلزم الكفر به، والله أن يجزيه عليه بما ملكه ما به يمتنع عن الدفع إليه. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
وأمكن أن يقال: ذلك فضل الله إلى عباده أن لم يُلزمهم يمثل ذلك طاعة الشيطان وعبادته ، إذ علم شدة ذلك عليهم ؛ على ما أكرمهم الله في حال العصيان بمعاداة الشيطان، وأنه لا أحد أبغض إليهم منه، ولا شيء أثقل على طباعهم وعقولهم مما فيه سروره بذلك على وجهين: أحدهما في طاعته وعبادته؛ فتجاوز الله عن العاجل بمنع اسم الطاعة والعبادة له؛ والثاني بإطماع المغفرة والتجاوز، بما آثر عداوة الشيطان في وقت عصيانه ورجاء رحمة رب العالمين المعروف بالكرم والجود الذي لم يزل يعودهم بإحسانه إليهم وإفضاله عليهم له الحمد على ذلك أوفره.
Also, every believer who disobeys God in something is like one driven to it, by what overcomes him of desire or anger or zeal or similar things by which he comes to it. When he does not intend to disobey the Lord or obey Satan, but becomes from the aspect you mentioned like one driven, then disbelief is not entailed by it, and God will requite him for it according to what He granted him by which he refrains from being driven to it. There is no power except with God. And it may be said: That is God's grace to His servants that He did not make them liable for such as obedience to Satan and worship of him, since He knew the severity of that upon them; according to how God honored them in the state of disobedience with enmity towards Satan, and that there is none more hateful to them than him, and nothing heavier on their natures and intellects than that which involves his pleasure in that, in two aspects: one is in his obedience and worship; so God overlooked in the immediate [world] by withholding the name of obedience and worship for him; and the second is by giving hope of forgiveness and overlooking, because of their preference for enmity towards Satan at the time of their disobedience and their hope for the mercy of the Lord of the worlds, known for generosity and bounty, who has not ceased to return to them with His goodness and favor upon them. To Him belongs the most abundant praise for that.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument (وأيضا) and an additional point about divine grace. The argument addresses situations where a believer falls into sin under compulsion from desire, anger, etc., without intending to disobey God or obey Satan. Such a person is 'driven' (مدفوع) and therefore not guilty of disbelief. God will judge according to the means He gave to resist. Then, an additional explanation (وأمكن أن يقال) highlights God's grace: He does not label such acts as obedience or worship of Satan, understanding human weakness. Two aspects of this grace are mentioned: 1) God withholds the name of obedience and worship from these acts in this world, preventing them from being considered true worship of Satan; 2) God gives hope of forgiveness because the believer still harbors enmity towards Satan even while sinning, hoping for God's mercy. This encourages repentance.

Key Terms
مدفوع
شهوة
عصيان
فضل الله
معاداة الشيطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any sin, even under compulsion, makes a person a disbeliever.
Correction: The passage clarifies that when a believer sins involuntarily without intending to obey Satan, disbelief does not follow; God's grace prevents it from being considered worship.

Checkpoint
According to the grace mentioned, what is the first aspect of God's favor regarding actions that please Satan?
A) He punishes them immediately.
B) He withholds the name of obedience and worship from them.
C) He rewards them for their intention.
D) He makes them forget their sin.

Key Takeaway
Even when believers sin involuntarily, God's grace prevents such acts from being labeled as worship of Satan, offering hope for forgiveness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a specific moment when you sinned because you were overcome by desire or anger. In that moment, did you feel that you were serving Satan? How does this lesson's teaching that God withholds the name of worship from such acts change your view of that failure? Will you now see it as a weakness rather than an allegiance?
?
The lesson says that even while sinning, believers maintain enmity towards Satan. Honestly, when you fall into sin, does your heart truly hate Shaytan and what he loves? Or do you sometimes find pleasure in the sin, aligning with his desires? This distinction determines whether you can hope for the grace mentioned here. Which is true of you?
?
God’s grace in this passage gives hope of forgiveness because He knows the severity of our struggle. Are you living in that hope, or are you paralyzed by guilt over sins you committed under compulsion? What would change in your relationship with God today if you fully believed that He has already withheld the label of 'worship of Satan' from those sins?

Faith and Disbelief

The Believer's Heart Sanctifies His Actions
Maturidi explains that a believer's firm conviction prevents his actions from being worship of Satan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a believer’s sinful actions cannot be classified as worship of Satan, based on the purity of his heart and intention.

Core Idea
A believer’s heart, fixed on God, cannot become a temple for Satan.

Imam Maturidi addresses a subtle theological concern: when a believer sins, does that count as worshipping Satan? This passage explains that the believer’s deep-seated conviction and recognition of God’s lordship sanctifies his actions, so even lapses remain within the fold of faith. Let’s explore how the heart’s allegiance guards against such attribution.

Guided Path
1
Understand the believer's heart state
Recognize the stages: belief in obedience to the Lord, knowledge of servitude, mindfulness of blessings, and perception of God's power and wisdom. This heart state is foundational.
These are not just intellectual but heartfelt convictions that shape action.
2
See how the heart restrains inclination
Because of this state, the believer naturally refrains from inclining to obey or even imagine worshipping other than God. The heart becomes guarded.
The text says 'كف أن تميل إلى طاعة من لا يكون طاعته طاعته' – the heart itself prevents such inclination.
3
Examine the case of sin due to desire
Even if the believer later commits a sin due to overwhelming desire, hope for mercy, or compulsion, the act cannot be diverted to obedience of another, because the heart’s intention remains with God at the moment of action.
The phrase 'وما ذكرته هو لازم قلبه وقت فعله' emphasizes the heart's state during the deed.
4
Contrast with the disbeliever
The disbeliever, whose basic belief is in other than God, has his actions attributed to the one who led him to that (Satan or the self). This highlights the decisive role of underlying conviction.
The passage ends with 'ولا قوة إلا بالله' – a reminder of divine enablement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإن العبد إذا اعتقد طاعة الرب، وعرف العبودية، وأشعر قلبه عظيم نعمه عليه وآلائه لديه ، ثم أراه عظيم سلطانه وقدرته بما ذكره حكمته في خلقه ونفاذ مشيئته فيه كف أن تميل إلى طاعة من لا يكون طاعته طاعته، وصانها عن توهم عبادة دونه . [ف]لم يجز صرف فعله الواقع منه - بعد أن اطمأن قلبه على هذا وصار ذا آثَرَ عنده الدنيا من والآخرة - لشهوة غلبته أو لرحمة يأملها أو لأمر دفعه إليها، [إلى] طاعة لغيره أو عبادة منه أحدا ،دونه، وما ذكرته هو لازم قلبه وقت فعله . وإنما يكون مثله من الكافر الذي اعتقد طاعة من دونه وعبادة مَن لا يستحقها، أن يُصرف ذلك إلى مَن به صار إلى ذلك من الشيطان أو النفس. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Afterwards, when the servant believes in obedience to the Lord, and knows servitude, and his heart is made to feel the greatness of His blessings upon him and His favors with him, then He shows him the greatness of His dominion and power through what He mentioned of His wisdom in creation and the execution of His will in him, he refrains from inclining to obedience of one whose obedience is not His obedience, and guards it from imagining worship of other than Him. So it is not permissible to divert his actual deed—after his heart is assured of this and he becomes one who prefers the world over the Hereafter due to desire that overcomes him or mercy he hopes for or a matter that drives him to it—to obedience of another or worship of anyone other than Him. And what I mentioned is the necessary state of his heart at the time of the deed. Rather, the likeness of that is from the disbeliever who believed in obedience to other than Him and worship of one who does not deserve it, that the deed is attributed to the one by whom he came to that, whether Satan or the self. There is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage describes the state of a true believer. When a believer has firm conviction in obedience to God, recognizes his servitude, is mindful of God's blessings, and perceives His power and wisdom, his heart naturally guards against inclining to obedience of anyone else. Therefore, even if he later commits a sin due to overcomeing desire, hope for mercy, or external compulsion, his action cannot be considered obedience or worship of another, because his heart's intention remains fixed on God. The passage contrasts this with a disbeliever, whose actions are rightly attributed to Satan or his own self because his belief is in other than God. The core idea is that a believer's inner conviction prevents his lapses from being categorised as worship of Satan.

Key Terms
اعتقاد
طاعة الرب
القلب
العبودية
الشيطان
النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might assume that any sinful act by a believer counts as worshipping Satan.
Correction: This passage shows that the believer's underlying faith and heart's intention change the category of the act; it is not worship of Satan because the heart remains fixed on obedience to God.

Checkpoint
What prevents a believer's sinful act from being considered worship of Satan according to this passage?
A) The act is minor.
B) The act was done secretly.
C) The believer's heart remains fixed on obedience to God.
D) The believer repents immediately.

Key Takeaway
A believer's actions are judged by the state of his heart; a heart devoted to God cannot produce acts of worship for other than Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you immediately assume that your heart has turned away from God? Or can you, like the believer described here, affirm that your underlying conviction remains with God despite the failure? Examine a recent sin: what was the state of your heart at that moment?
?
If your heart is truly settled on God, why do you still sin? Is it due to desire, hope for mercy, or external compulsion? Which of these is most dominant in your life, and what does that reveal about your need for God's power?
?
Consider the disbeliever's state: his actions are attributed to Satan because his heart's conviction is for other than God. Do you ever find that your heart's reliance leans toward created things—people, status, comfort—more than God? How might that affect how you view your actions?

Faith Is More Than Words: Inner Belief as the Core of Faith
Maturidi refutes the view that faith is only verbal confession using Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that faith cannot be merely verbal confession but must include inner conviction, using Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Faith is a matter of the heart, not just the tongue.

Some theologians claimed that faith is only verbal confession. Imam al-Maturidi refutes this by citing Quranic verses that distinguish between outward submission and inward belief. This lesson examines his argument from revelation, showing that true faith requires heartfelt conviction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Notice how Maturidi structures his refutation.
The passage is cut off at the end, but the main argument is clear.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
Maturidi cites verses about the hypocrites, the Bedouins, and the believing women. For each, note what aspect of faith is being highlighted.
The hypocrites said they believed but their hearts did not; the Bedouins were told faith had not entered their hearts.
3
Contrast with the wrong view
Reflect on the difference between the claim that faith is only verbal and Maturidi's evidence. Ask yourself: why can't a mere verbal confession be sufficient?
This helps internalize the core doctrine.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الخامس ] مسائل الإيمان والإسلام] مسألة الإقرار والتصديق في الإيمان ] قال قوم: الإيمان هو الإقرار باللسان خاصة وليس في / القلب شيء". { قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : } ونحن نقول وبالله التوفيق أحق ما يكون به الإيمان القلوب بالسمع والعقل جميعا. أ - أما السمع فما قال الله تعالى في المنافقين الذين قالوا آمنا بأفواههم ولم تؤمن قلوبهم ، وقال : قالت الأعراب آمنا قل لم تؤمنوا ولكن قولوا أسلمنا ولما يدخل الإيمان في قلوبكم [الحجرات، ١٤/٤٩] أبطل أن يكون قولهم إيمانا إذا لم تؤمن قلوبهم، وقال: يمنون عليك أن أسلموا قل لا تمنّوا علي إسلامكم بل الله يمن عليكم أن هداكم للإيمان إن كنتم صادقین﴾ [الحجرات، ١٧/٤٩]، فأخبر أنهم لو كانوا بما ادعوا من الإيمان مؤمنين - بهداية الله - لكانوا مؤمنين لو صدقوا " . ولو لم يكن الإيمان إلا باللسان لكان إذا نطقوا به فقد صدقوا. وقال تعالى: يا أيها الذين آمنوا إذا جاءكم المؤمنات مهاجرات فامتحنوهن الله أعلم بإيمانهن ﴾ [الممتحنة، ١٠/٦٠] الآية ؛ أخبر أن الله تعالى أعلم بإيمانهن. ولو كان الإيمان ليس إلا القول باللسان لكان كل سامع واحدا في العلم. وقال تعالى: ويحلفون بالله إنهم
Chapter Five: Issues of Faith and Islam. Issue: Affirmation and Confirmation in Faith. Some people said: Faith is only verbal confession, and there is nothing in the heart. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: And we say, with Allah is success, the most deserving thing by which faith occurs in the hearts is through hearing and reason together. As for hearing, the words of Allah regarding the hypocrites who said, 'We believe with their mouths, but their hearts did not believe.' And He said: 'The Bedouins said: "We believe." Say: "You have not believed, but rather say: "We have submitted," for faith has not yet entered your hearts."' [Al-Hujurat 49:14] He nullified that their saying is faith if their hearts do not believe. And He said: 'They consider it a favor to you that they have submitted. Say: "Do not consider your submission a favor to me; rather, Allah confers favor upon you that He has guided you to faith, if you should be truthful."' [Al-Hujurat 49:17] So He informed that if they were believers in what they claimed of faith — by Allah's guidance — they would be believers if they were truthful. And if faith were only by the tongue, then if they uttered it they would have been truthful. And He said: 'O you who have believed, when the believing women come to you as emigrants, examine them. Allah knows best their faith.' [Al-Mumtahana 60:10] — the verse; He informed that Allah is most knowing of their faith. And if faith were only speech by the tongue, then every hearer would be equal in knowledge. And He said: 'And they swear by Allah that they are...'
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that faith (إيمان) is solely verbal confession (إقرار باللسان), a position attributed to the Karramiyya. Abu Mansur al-Maturidi responds by affirming that faith occurs in the hearts through both revealed evidence (السمع) and reason (العقل). He begins with the scriptural evidence (السمع): first, the verse about hypocrites who said 'we believe' with their mouths but their hearts did not believe, showing that their verbal confession is not accepted as faith. Second, the verse about the Bedouins (الأعراب) who claimed faith but were told they have not truly believed; instead they are to say they have submitted (أسلمنا), indicating that faith requires entry into the heart. Third, the verse about the migrating women where Allah knows their faith best; if faith were only speech, every human would have equal knowledge of it. The author also notes that if faith were only by the tongue, then anyone who utters the words would be truthful, but the Quran exposes the hypocrisy of some. The passage is cut off but the argument is clear: faith must be a conviction of the heart, not just a verbal statement.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Simply saying the shahada makes one a believer regardless of inner state.
Correction: This passage shows that inner belief (conviction of the heart) is necessary; verbal confession alone is not sufficient, as the hypocrites and Bedouins demonstrate.

Checkpoint

A) Their faith is accepted because they said 'we believe'.
B) Faith is only verbal confession.
C) They are true believers despite their words.
D) Their statement 'we believe' is not accepted because faith has not entered their hearts.

Key Takeaway
True faith (iman) is a conviction of the heart, not merely a verbal statement; the Quran exposes those who claim faith with their tongues while their hearts are empty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I believe' in your prayers or conversations, do you ever sense a gap between your words and what your heart truly holds? This lesson exposes that as hypocrisy—are you willing to examine your own heart right now and ask Allah to purify it?
?
Consider a time you performed an outward act of worship while your mind was elsewhere. Did you assume that the act alone was accepted? This passage teaches that Allah looks at the heart—what one area of your faith life are you merely going through the motions in?
?
If your faith were tested today, would the words of your mouth and the state of your heart align? Imagine standing before Allah with only your inner reality—what would you want to change starting this moment?

Quranic Proofs That Hypocrites Are Kuffar
Quranic proofs that hypocrites are kuffar in reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verbal profession of hypocrites does not constitute true faith, as proven by multiple Quranic verses that show their hearts contradict their tongues.

Core Idea
True faith requires the heart's assent; mere words without inner conviction are lies.

Imam Maturidi presents a powerful scriptural argument that the hypocrites, despite outwardly claiming Islam, are in reality disbelievers. This lesson examines the Quranic evidence he marshals, from verses that call them liars to those that warn them of the lowest depths of Hell. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a correct conception of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the argument.
Notice how many Quranic verses are cited.
2
Identify the key Quranic proofs
Look at each quoted verse and note what it says about the hypocrites. The author uses them to show that their faith is not genuine.
Pay special attention to verses 2:8, 4:65, and 63:1.
3
Understand the deception argument
The author argues that calling the hypocrites' profession 'faith' would mean faith can be attained by deception, which is absurd.
This is a logical argument from the nature of faith.
4
Grasp the linguistic definition
The author defines iman as tasdiq (assent) in language. Since the hypocrites' hearts reject, their verbal claim is a lie.
This shows the importance of inner conviction.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that faith cannot be described with mockery and deception; therefore hypocrites are disbelievers.
How does this affect our understanding of who is a believer?

لمنكم وما هم منكم الآية، أخبر أنهم كذبوا في ذلك. وقال : فلا وربك لا يؤمنون، ولو لم يكن غير اللسان لم يكن لينفي إيمانهم بوجود الحرج في الأنفس. وقال تعالى: فمن ما ملكت أيمانكم من فتياتكم المؤمنات، ثم قال: والله أعلم بإيمانكم، بين أن الإيمان حقيقة حيث يعلم الله به وحده. وقال تعالى: ومن الناس من يقول آمنا بالله وباليوم الآخر وما هم بمؤمنين، نفي أن يكون الذي قالوا بألسنتهم إيمانا إذا خالفت قلوبهم ذلك. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
ثم إن الله عز وجل وعد للمؤمنين الثواب الدائم، وأخبر في المنافقين أنهم في الدرك الأسفل من النار. فلو كان ما أظهروا إيمانا في الحقيقة لكان حقه على الموعود الجنة، لا الزيادة على عقوبة الكفر. وقال تعالى : يخادعون الله والذين آمنوا الآية، صير إيمانهم الذي أظهروا مخادعة الله. فمن زعم أن مرتبة دين الإسلام والإيمان بالأنبياء وبالله وبما أرسلهم به يحصل على مخادعة الله فهو عظيم القول في دين الله، جاهل بربه. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقال الله عز وجل: سواء عليهم استغفرت لهم أم لم تستغفر لهم الآية، وقال تعالى: استغفر لهم أو لا تستغفر لهم الآية، وقال تعالى: وما منعهم أن تقبل منهم نفقاتهم إلا أنهم كفروا بالله وبرسوله، وغير ذلك مما أخبر الله عن المنافقين أنهم كفروا؛
والكفر ضد الإيمان، وبالإيمان ننتهى عن الكفر. وقال الله تعالى: وإن ينتهوا يغفر لهم ما قد سلف، وقال تعالى : ومن يفعل ذلك يلق أثامًا، إلى آخر تلك الآيات.
وإذ ثبت أن المنافقين كفرة في التحقيق، كذبة في قولهم، بما قال الله: والله يشهد إن المنافقين لكاذبون، وقال: يوم يبعثهم الله جميعا الآية؛ أخبر أنهم كذبة، فجعل قول الإسلام منهم على جحود بالقلب كذبًا. فمن جعل ذلك إيمانا - والإيمان في اللغة هو التصديق ـ فقد جعل الشيء ضده، وذلك فاسد. وقال: لا تعتذروا قد كفرتم بعد إيمانكم الآية، وقال: سيحلفون بالله لكم إذا انقلبتم إليهم الآية، وقال: ليخرجن الأعز منها الأذل والله العزة ولرسوله وللمؤمنين ولكن المنافقين لا يعلمون؛ أخبر أنهم كفرة، وأنهم لا يعلمون لمن العزة، وأنها لمن ذكر، ولو كانوا منهم لكانت لهم. ولا قوة إلا بالله. مع ما جعل الله ذلك منهم استهزاء ومخادعة وسخرية وأوجب لهم جزاء ذلك، ولم يجز أن يكون الإيمان هذا وصفه. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The verse: 'they are not of you, nor are they of them' [Quran 9:56], He informed that they lied in that. And He said: 'But no, by your Lord, they will not believe' [Quran 4:65], and if there were nothing other than the tongue, He would not have negated their belief by the existence of constraint in the souls. And the Exalted said: 'so from what your right hands possess of your believing maids' [Quran 4:25], then He said: 'and Allah knows best your faith' [Quran 4:25], He made clear that faith is a reality where Allah alone knows it. And the Exalted said: 'And among people are those who say we believe in Allah and the Last Day, but they are not believers' [Quran 2:8], He negated that what they said with their tongues is faith when their hearts contradict that. And there is no power except with Allah. Then Allah Almighty promised believers eternal reward, and informed about the hypocrites that they are in the lowest depths of the Fire. So if what they displayed were faith in reality, its right would be the promised Paradise, not the increase over the punishment of disbelief. And the Exalted said: 'they deceive Allah and those who believe' [Quran 2:9], He made the faith they displayed a deception of Allah. So whoever claims that the rank of the religion of Islam and faith in the prophets and in Allah and in what He sent them with is attained by deception of Allah, he is great in speech concerning the religion of Allah, ignorant of his Lord. And there is no power except with Allah. And Allah Almighty said: 'It is the same for them whether you ask forgiveness for them or do not ask forgiveness for them' [Quran 63:6], and the Exalted said: 'Ask forgiveness for them or do not ask forgiveness for them' [Quran 9:80], and the Exalted said: 'And nothing prevents their expenditures from being accepted from them except that they disbelieved in Allah and His Messenger' [Quran 9:54], and other than that which Allah informed about the hypocrites that they disbelieved. And disbelief is the opposite of faith, and by faith we are restrained from disbelief. And Allah the Exalted said: 'And if they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them' [Quran 8:38], and the Exalted said: 'And whoever does that will meet a penalty' [Quran 25:68], to the end of those verses. And since it is established that the hypocrites are disbelievers in reality, liars in their statement, by what Allah said: 'And Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are indeed liars' [Quran 63:1], and He said: 'On the day when Allah will raise them all' [Quran 58:18] verse; He informed that they are liars, so He made their statement of Islam, along with denial in the heart, a lie. So whoever makes that faith—and faith in language is tasdiq (belief/assent)—has made a thing its opposite, and that is corrupt. And He said: 'Do not make excuses; you have disbelieved after your faith' [Quran 9:66] verse, and He said: 'They will swear by Allah to you when you return to them' [Quran 9:95] verse, and He said: 'The mightier will surely drive out the weaker from it, and might belongs to Allah and His Messenger and the believers, but the hypocrites do not know' [Quran 63:8]; He informed that they are disbelievers, and that they do not know to whom might belongs, and that it belongs to whom He mentioned, and if they were among them they would have it. And there is no power except with Allah. Along with what Allah made of that from them: mockery, deception, and ridicule, and He obligated for them the recompense of that, and it is not permissible that faith be described in this way. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage is a Quranic proof that the hypocrites are disbelievers in reality, despite their verbal profession of faith. The author cites multiple verses to demonstrate that their tongues contradict their hearts. Beginning with Quran 9:56, Allah informs that hypocrites lie when they claim to be part of the believers. Then Quran 4:65 shows that true faith requires an open heart, not just verbal assent. The verse Quran 2:8 explicitly negates faith for those who say with their tongues what their hearts do not believe. The author then argues that if their verbal profession were real faith, they would be promised Paradise, yet Allah warns them of the lowest depths of Hell (Quran 4:145). Their profession is described as deception (Quran 2:9), so claiming that Islam and faith can be attained by deception is a grave error. Subsequent verses (Quran 63:6, 9:80, 9:54) emphasize that their disbelief prevents acceptance of their deeds. The author then defines faith linguistically as tasdiq (assent), showing that the hypocrites are liars, not believers. Their claim to faith is contradictory because they deny in their hearts. The passage concludes that Allah describes them as disbelievers who mock and deceive, and such description cannot apply to true faith.

Iman Is in the Heart: Proof from Quran and Hadith
Proof that the heart is the locus of iman from Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the heart is the true locus of iman, based on Quranic and prophetic evidence, and how forced utterances do not affect genuine faith.

Core Idea
Faith lives in the heart, not on the tongue.

This lesson delves into a foundational argument from Imam Maturidi that the seat of faith is the heart. Using a key Quranic verse about forced apostasy, he shows that mere verbal denial does not constitute disbelief if the heart remains firm. He also addresses a potential objection from a well-known hadith, clarifying its scope.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Imam Maturidi uses a concise, argumentative style.
2
Identify the key Quranic proof
Locate Quran 16:106 in the passage. Understand its context: it deals with someone forced to utter disbelief while their heart is at peace with faith. Allah does not consider that utterance as actual disbelief.
This verse is the main evidence that the heart is the locus of iman.
3
Understand the counterargument
The passage mentions a hadith: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they testify...' Some might think this proves faith is only verbal testimony.
Imam Maturidi anticipates this objection to strengthen his position.
4
See the refutation
Imam Maturidi argues that the hadith is not proof that verbal testimony alone is faith; rather, it pertains to the outward ruling in this world. True faith is in the heart.
The refutation distinguishes between worldly rulings and the reality of iman.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that the heart is the locus of faith. Reflect on why this distinction matters for understanding who is a believer and the nature of iman.
This lesson establishes a core principle of Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال الله : إلا من أكره وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان لم يجعل لهم كفرا باللسان إذا لم يكن عبارة عن القلب، ومنع ذلك بإيمان القلب، فثبت أن القلب هو موضع الإيمان.
وبالله التوفيق. وليس بما يُقاتلون إلى أن يشهدوا باللسان دليل [على] أن ذلك هو الإيمان، أو لا إيمان
And Allah said: 'except one who is compelled while his heart is at rest with faith' [Quran 16:106], He did not make for them disbelief by the tongue when it is not an expression of the heart, and He prevented that by the faith of the heart, so it is established that the heart is the locus of faith. And with Allah is success. And it is not that they are fought until they testify with the tongue a proof of that being faith, or no faith.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage presents the positive proof that faith resides in the heart, not merely on the tongue. The author cites Quran 16:106, which addresses the case of someone forced to utter disbelief while his heart remains firm in faith. Allah does not consider such an utterance as actual disbelief because it does not come from the heart. Conversely, the verse implies that if the heart were not firm, the utterance would be disbelief. Thus, the heart is the seat of faith. The author then addresses a common counterargument based on the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they testify that there is no god but Allah...' Some might argue that this proves faith is merely verbal testimony. The author refutes this by stating that the hadith is not proof that verbal testimony alone constitutes faith; rather, it is about the outward ruling in this world. True faith is in the heart, as the Quranic verse demonstrates. The passage concludes by affirming that the heart is the locus of faith.

إيمان
لسان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the hadith about fighting until people testify proves that faith is only verbal testimony.
Correction: Imam Maturidi shows that the hadith concerns outward rulings in this world, not the reality of iman. True faith is in the heart, as established by Quran 16:106.

Checkpoint

B) The verse about forced apostasy (Quran 16:106)

D) The linguistic definition alone

Key Takeaway
The heart is the locus of iman; the tongue only expresses what is in the heart.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you face a test—whether minor social pressure or major threat—what is the condition of your heart? Are you preparing now so that when the moment comes, your heart will be 'mutma'in'?

Faith is in the Heart: The Core Proof
Maturidi proves that faith resides in the heart, using Quranic verses on hypocrites and compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam Maturidi proves that true faith (iman) is primarily an affirmation of the heart, not merely verbal confession.

Core Idea
Faith is heart-affirmation, not a tongue-declaration.

Imam Maturidi begins by establishing that faith and disbelief are opposites, then uses the example of hypocrites to show that mere verbal claims are insufficient. He argues that faith linguistically means affirmation (tasdiq), and since hypocrites deny in their hearts, their speech is a lie, not faith. Then he cites the Quranic verse on compulsion to conclusively prove that the heart is the true locus of faith.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opposition of iman and kufr
Read the opening sentence where Maturidi states that kufr is the opposite of iman, and that iman prevents kufr. Notice how he frames the discussion.
This sets the stage for the argument.
2
Analyze the hypocrite argument
Follow how Maturidi uses the verses about hypocrites to show that their verbal Islam is a lie because their hearts deny. This demonstrates that faith cannot be mere speech.
The linguistic definition of iman as tasdiq (affirmation) is key here.
3
Learn from the compulsion verse
Examine the verse 'except one who is forced while his heart is at rest with faith' (16:106). Maturidi argues that if the tongue alone mattered, the coerced person would be a disbeliever; but Allah does not count that as kufr, proving faith is in the heart.
This is the decisive proof that the heart is the locus of faith.

والكفر ضد الإيمان، وبالإيمان ننتهى عن الكفر. وقال الله تعالى: وإن ينتهوا يغفر لهم ما قد سلف [الأنفال، ۳۸/۸]، وقال تعالى: ﴿ومن يفعل ذلك يلق أثامًا﴾ [الفرقان، ٦٨/٢٥]، إلى آخر تلك الآيات. وإذ ثبت أن المنافقين كَفَرة في التحقيق، كذبة في قولهم، بما قال الله: ﴿والله يشهد إن المنافقين لكاذبون﴾ [المنافقون، ١/٦٣]، وقال: ﴿يوم يبعثهم الله جميعًا﴾ الآية؛ أخبر أنهم كَذَبَة، فجعل قول الإسلام منهم على جحود بالقلب كذبًا. فمن جعل ذلك إيمانًا - والإيمان في اللغة هو التصديق ـ فقد جعل الشيء ضده، وذلك فاسد. وقال: ﴿لا تعتذروا قد كفرتم بعد إيمانكم﴾ [التوبة، ٦٦/٩] الآية، وقال: ﴿سيحلفون بالله لكم إذا انقلبتم إليهم﴾ الآية، وقال: ﴿لَيُخْرِجَنّ الأعز منها الأذل والله العزة ولرسوله وللمؤمنين ولكن المنافقين لا يعلمون﴾ [المنافقون، ٨/٦٣]؛ أخبر أنهم كفرة، وأنهم لا يعلمون لمن العزة، وأنها لمن ذكر، ولو كانوا منهم لكانت لهم ولا قوة إلا بالله . مع ما جعل الله ذلك منهم استهزاء ومخادعة وسخرية وأوجب لهم جزاء ذلك، ولم يجز أن يكون الإيمان هذا وصفه. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقد قال الله : ﴿إلا من أكره وقلبه مطمئن بالإيمان﴾ لم يجعل لهم كفرًا باللسان إذا لم يكن عبارة عن القلب، ومنع ذلك بإيمان القلب، فثبت أن القلب هو موضع الإيمان. وبالله التوفيق. وليس بما يُقاتلون إلى أن يشهدوا باللسان دليل [على] أن ذلك هو الإيمان، أو لا إيمان بالقلوب؛ بل ذلك منهم دليل الإيمان وعبارة عنه . فيقبل قولهم في الأحكام الظاهرة بحق العبارة بما لا سبيل لنا إلى حقيقة العلم به. وعلى ذلك عامة الأمور بين الخلق محمولة على ما يحتمله وسعهم من المعارف وإن كانت لها حقائق غيرها. مع ما كان في الذي بيّنا دلالة ذلك. وكذلك الأمر المتوارث في التفصيل بين الكفر[ة] وبين المؤمنين بالأعلام وأنواع الزي، أو المخالطة مع الأهل، وإن لم يكن تلك بكفر ولا إسلام، فمثله أمر العبارة باللسان. وعلى هذا ما بيّنا من الآيات في العلم بالإيمان وأمر القلوب فيما جاء به النصوص، فمثله الذي نحن فيه. والله أعلم. وعلى ذلك أمر المكره على الكفر، وقول نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «إنما يعبر عما في قلبه لسانه»؛ وعلى ما ذكرتُ أمر الإملاك والشهادات وأنواع المذاهب في الأديان بما علمه [من] ذلك بالأمور الظاهرة، فمثله حكم القبول وقد تجد : الله أمر بأن يقاتل ليعطوا الجزية، وأن يجاروا إلى أن يسمعوا كلام الله . وفي ذلك التّرك بين المسلمين يتعيشون لينظروا في أمورهم ويتدبروا في أحكامهم فيعلموا بذلك حقائقها - وإن كان لا يُحتمل تأسيسها على ما فيها من تأليف القلوب ودفع التظالم وأنواع الفساد إلا بالله - ليطمئن قلوبهم بالإيمان وتحتمل أنفسهم الإجابة إلى الإسلام، فمثله في الذين أظهروا الإيمان بالله وأجابوا المؤمنين إلى ما عندهم من الأحكام. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يقال لهم: فإن كان ما يُقبل منهم من الإيمان في ظواهر الأحكام باللسان دليلاً
Disbelief (kufr) is the opposite of faith (iman), and by faith we refrain from disbelief. And Allah Most High said: 'And if they desist, what is past will be forgiven them' (al-Anfal 8:38), and Most High said: 'And whoever does that will meet a penalty' (al-Furqan 25:68), to the end of those verses. And since it is established that the hypocrites (munafiqun) are disbelievers in reality, liars in their speech, by what Allah said: 'And Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are indeed liars' (al-Munafiqun 63:1), and He said: 'On the Day when Allah will raise them all' the verse; He informed that they are liars, so He made their utterance of Islam (qawl al-islam) from them, upon denial in the heart, a lie. Whoever makes that faith—while faith in language is affirmation (tasdiq)—has made the thing its opposite, and that is corrupt. And He said: 'Do not make excuses; you have disbelieved after your faith' (al-Tawba 9:66) the verse, and He said: 'They will swear by Allah to you when you return to them' the verse, and He said: 'Indeed, the honored one will expel the despised one from it, and to Allah belongs honor, and to His Messenger, and to the believers, but the hypocrites do not know' (al-Munafiqun 63:8); He informed that they are disbelievers, and that they do not know to whom honor belongs, and that it belongs to whomever He mentioned, and if they were among them it would be theirs—and there is no power except through Allah. Along with what Allah made of that from them as mockery, deception, and ridicule, and He obligated for them the recompense for that, and it is not permissible that faith has this description. And there is no power except through Allah. And Allah said: 'Except for one who is forced while his heart is at rest with faith' (al-Nahl 16:106); He did not make for them disbelief (kufr) by the tongue when it is not an expression of the heart, and He prevented that by faith of the heart. So it is established that the heart is the locus of faith. And with Allah is success. And it is not what they fight until they testify by the tongue a proof that that is faith, or that there is no faith in hearts; rather that from them is a sign (dalil) of faith and an expression (ibara) of it. So their statement is accepted in outward rulings by right of expression, since we have no way to true knowledge of it. And upon that, most matters among creation are carried on what their capacity of knowledge can bear, even if they have realities other than that. Along with what was in what we clarified of indication of that. And likewise the inherited practice in distinguishing between disbelievers and believers by signs and types of appearance, or mixing with family, even if that is not disbelief nor Islam, so likewise is the matter of expression by the tongue. And upon this is what we clarified of verses concerning knowledge of faith and the matter of hearts regarding what the texts brought, so likewise is what we are in. And Allah knows best. And upon that is the matter of the one forced into disbelief, and the saying of the Prophet of Allah, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, the tongue expresses what is in the heart.' And upon what I mentioned is the matter of marriages, testimonies, and types of schools in religions by what He knows of that through outward matters, so likewise is the ruling of acceptance. And you may find that Allah commanded that one fight so that they give the jizya, and that they be granted protection until they hear the speech of Allah. And in that, leaving among Muslims to live so that they look into their affairs and ponder over their rulings, so that by that they know their realities—even if it is not possible to establish them on what they contain of composing hearts and preventing injustice and types of corruption except through Allah—so that their hearts are at ease with faith and their souls are able to respond to Islam. So likewise regarding those who outwardly showed faith in Allah and answered the believers regarding what they have of rulings. And there is no power except through Allah. Then it is said to them: For if what is accepted from them of faith in outward rulings by the tongue is a sign...
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the true locus of faith (iman) is the heart, not mere verbal declaration. Maturidi proceeds in a structured argument: 1) He begins by stating that disbelief (kufr) is the opposite of faith, and that faith prevents disbelief, citing Quranic verses about the hypocrites who are declared disbelievers despite their verbal claims. 2) He argues that hypocrites' testimony of faith is a lie because their hearts deny it, so it cannot be real faith—faith linguistically means affirmation (tasdiq), so calling a lie faith is contradictory. 3) He then uses the verse on compulsion (Quran 16:106) to prove that the heart is the seat of faith: when one is forced to utter disbelief while the heart remains steadfast, he is not considered a disbeliever. This shows that the tongue's speech is not the reality of faith; rather faith is in the heart. 4) He then addresses the practical acceptance of verbal testimony in Islamic law: although faith is essentially in the heart, we accept people's declarations outwardly because we have no access to inner hearts. This is like other matters in life where we rely on outward signs. 5) He supports this with the hadith 'the tongue expresses what is in the heart' and examples from marriage, testimony, and treatment of dhimmis. 6) He concludes that the acceptance of verbal Islam in worldly rulings does not mean that true faith is merely speech; it is only a sign or expression. The argument guards against the error of equating outward confession with inward faith.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الكفر
المنافقون
التصديق
القلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that simply uttering the shahada makes one a believer in God's sight, even if the heart denies.
Correction: Maturidi shows that hypocrites' speech is a lie, and the compulsion verse proves that faith is in the heart, not the tongue.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Maturidi in this passage, what is the primary locus of faith (iman)?
A) The tongue
B) The heart
C) Both heart and tongue equally
D) Actions

Key Takeaway
True faith is the heart's affirmation, not the tongue's utterance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada or make du'a, is your heart truly affirming each word, or are your lips moving while your mind wanders? Today, before any prayer or dhikr, pause for five seconds and consciously bring your heart into agreement with your tongue.
?
Think of a moment you felt pressured to hide your beliefs or even say something contrary to your faith. Did you fear that your spoken words made you a hypocrite? This lesson teaches that the heart is what matters. What can you do this week to strengthen your heart's conviction so that even if your tongue falters, your faith remains unshaken?
?
The hypocrites are condemned because their hearts were empty while they spoke of faith. In what area of your life—your relationships, your work, your private thoughts—is there a gap between what you say you believe and what your heart truly holds? Write down one specific step you will take tonight to close that gap.

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Outward Testimony: A Sign, Not the Reality
Maturidi explains that outward verbal acceptance of faith is a legal sign, not the reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Maturidi, outward verbal testimony is accepted in Islamic law only as a sign (dalil) of inner faith, not as the reality itself.

Core Idea
Outward speech is a sign of faith, not faith itself.

After establishing that faith is in the heart, Maturidi addresses a practical question: why do we accept people's verbal declarations of faith in legal rulings? He explains that verbal testimony is accepted as an expression (ibara) and a sign (dalil) of faith, because we cannot access inner hearts. He supports this with the hadith 'the tongue expresses what is in the heart' and examples from marriage, testimony, and treatment of non-Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Understand that testimony is accepted as a sign
Read how Maturidi argues that fighting is not to ensure inner faith but to get a sign. The verbal testimony is a sign (dalil) of faith, not faith itself.
This distinguishes the legal ruling from the reality.
2
Learn from the hadith and examples
Examine the hadith 'the tongue expresses what is in the heart' and the examples of marriage and testimony. These show that outward expressions are accepted as indicators.
They are not the reality but are sufficient for legal purposes.
3
See the practical application in Islamic law
Consider how this principle applies to jizya, marriage, and other rulings. The outward acceptance is enough for worldly dealings, even though the true state of the heart is known to Allah.
This reconciles the inner reality of faith with the outer legal system.

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the true locus of faith (iman) is the heart, not mere verbal declaration. According to Maturidi, why is verbal testimony accepted in Islamic legal rulings?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
8 min
Outward Profession as a Sign of Inner Faith
Maturidi argues that verbal confession is a sign of inner faith, not its reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that verbal confession is a sign of inner faith and not its reality, and how this principle applies to worldly rulings.

Core Idea
Verbal confession is accepted as a sign of faith because we cannot access the heart.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses a central question: given that true faith resides in the heart, why do we judge people based on their verbal declarations? He explains that our acceptance is based on the principle that outward expressions serve as indicators of inner states, and in worldly matters we rely on these signs since we have no direct knowledge of the heart. This aligns with prophetic teachings and inherited practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Try to grasp the overall argument without overanalyzing.
2
Identify the core principle
Notice Maturidi's key statement: 'we have no way to true knowledge of it' (the heart). This is the foundation for accepting outward confession.
This principle appears early in the passage.
3
Examine the supporting examples
List the examples Maturidi gives: inherited practice (dress), the hadith about the tongue expressing the heart, rulings on marriage, testimony, jizya, and the case of coercion.
Each example reinforces that we judge by apparent signs.
4
Reflect on the broader application
Consider how this principle applies to general matters among creation: we accept what is apparent even if deeper realities differ.
5
Address the common misconception
Many think verbal confession alone defines faith. Maturidi clarifies that it is a sign, not the reality of faith itself.
This distinction is crucial for understanding his position.
