بالقلوب؛ بل ذلك منهم دليل الإيمان وعبارة عنه. فيقبل قولهم في الأحكام الظاهرة بحق العبارة بما لا سبيل لنا إلى حقيقة العلم به. وعلى ذلك عامة الأمور بين الخلق محمولة على ما يحتمله وسعهم من المعارف وإن كانت لها حقائق غيرها. مع ما كان في الذي بيّنا دلالة ذلك. وكذلك الأمر المتوارث في التفصيل بين الكفار وبين المؤمنين بالأعلام وأنواع الزي، أو المخالطة مع الأهل، وإن لم يكن تلك بكفر ولا إسلام، فمثله أمر العبارة باللسان. وعلى هذا ما بينا من الآيات في العلم بالإيمان وأمر القلوب فيما جاء به النصوص، فمثله الذي نحن فيه. والله أعلم. وعلى ذلك أمر المكره على الكفر، وقول نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إنما يعبر عما في قلبه لسانه»؛ وعلى ما ذكرتُ أمر الإملاك والشهادات وأنواع المذاهب في الأديان بما علم ذلك بالأمور الظاهرة، فمثله حكم القبول. وقد تجد: الله أمر بأن يقاتل ليعطوا الجزية، وأن يجاروا إلى أن يسمعوا كلام الله. وفي ذلك التّرك بين المسلمين يتعيشون لينظروا في أمورهم ويتدبروا في أحكامهم فيعلموا بذلك حقائقها - وإن كان لا يُحتمل تأسيسها على ما فيها من تأليف القلوب ودفع التظالم وأنواع الفساد إلا بالله - ليطمئن قلوبهم بالإيمان وتحتمل أنفسهم الإجابة إلى الإسلام، فمثله في الذين أظهروا الإيمان بالله وأجابوا المؤمنين إلى ما عندهم من الأحكام. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
With hearts; rather that from them is a sign of faith and an expression of it. So their statement is accepted in apparent rulings by right of expression, since we have no way to true knowledge of it. And upon that, general matters among creation are carried according to what their capacity of knowledge can bear, even if they have other realities. Along with that which we have clarified of its indication. Similarly, the inherited practice of distinguishing between the disbeliever and the believer by signs and types of attire or mixing with family, even if that is not disbelief nor Islam, so similarly is the matter of verbal expression. And upon this, what we have clarified from the verses concerning knowledge of faith and the matter of hearts according to what the texts have brought, so similarly is that which we are in. And God knows best. And upon that is the matter of the one coerced into disbelief, and the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Indeed the tongue expresses what is in his heart'; and upon what I have mentioned concerning the matter of marriages and testimonies and various schools in religions by which it is known from apparent matters, so similarly is the ruling of acceptance. And you find that God commanded to fight so that they give the jizya, and to give asylum until they hear the word of God. And in that is leaving among Muslims to live together to look into their affairs and ponder their rulings so that they may know their realities thereby - even if their foundation is not possible except through God's bringing together of hearts and repelling oppression and types of corruption - so that their hearts may be reassured with faith and their souls may bear the response to Islam, so similarly is the case of those who have shown faith in God and responded to the believers with what they have of rulings. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument about the relationship between outward verbal confession and inner faith. Maturidi states that we judge people by their apparent statements because we have no direct access to their inner hearts. He supports this with examples from inherited practice (distinguishing believers by dress), the hadith that the tongue expresses the heart, and the rulings on marriage, testimony, and jizya. The key point is that in worldly matters, we accept outward declarations, even though true faith resides in the heart. This does not negate inner faith; rather, the outward is a sign of it.

Why Hypocrites Are Denied Forgiveness Despite Confession
Objection and answer: if verbal confession is accepted, why punish hypocrites?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological reasoning behind why hypocrites, despite verbal confession, are not considered true believers and are denied eternal rewards.

Core Idea
Outward confession does not guarantee true faith or afterlife reward.

This passage presents an objection: if we accept verbal confession as sufficient for worldly rulings, why are hypocrites denied forgiveness? Imam Maturidi responds by distinguishing between outward acceptance and inner reality, showing that hypocrites do not truly worship, proving they lack genuine faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Notice how the objection is posed and the answer is given.
Focus on the logical structure: if... then... why not...?
2
Identify the objection
The opponent argues: if verbal confession alone is sufficient for faith in worldly rulings, then hypocrites who confess should also receive the promised rewards of the afterlife. Identify this conditional argument.
3
Understand Maturidi's answer
Imam Maturidi responds by pointing out that hypocrites do not truly worship in reality, nor do they attain virtue with God. Their outward confession does not earn them the afterlife rewards. This proves they are not true believers.
The key distinction is between apparent rulings (worldly) and true faith (which requires inner sincerity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: فإن كان ما يُقبل منهم من الإيمان في ظواهر الأحكام باللسان دليلاً على أنه هو خاصة. فلم حُرموا به الغفران والموعود على الإيمان من النعيم الدائم والثواب الجزيل؟ ثم بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة في الحقيقة ولا ينالون بها فضيلة عند الله دليل على أنهم ليسوا بمؤمنين. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then it is said to them: If what is accepted from them of faith in the apparent rulings by the tongue is a proof that it is solely [verbal], then why are they denied by it forgiveness and what is promised for faith of eternal bliss and great reward? Then, because they are not entitled to worship in reality nor do they attain virtue with God, that is proof that they are not believers. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer unit. The opponent argues: if we accept verbal confession as sufficient for worldly rulings, then hypocrites who confess should also receive the rewards of faith. Maturidi answers that hypocrites do not actually worship in reality nor attain virtue, proving they are not true believers. Thus, verbal confession alone does not earn them the afterlife reward; it only affects worldly judgments.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That outward verbal confession of faith guarantees salvation and entrance into Paradise in the afterlife.
Correction: Hypocrites may confess verbally but are denied forgiveness and reward because their confession lacks inner sincerity and true worship, showing that genuine faith requires both inward conviction and outward action accepted by God.

Checkpoint

Outward Actions Determine Worldly Rulings
Maturidi cites verses to prove outward actions determine worldly rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses about fighting to argue that outward profession, not inner belief, is the basis for worldly rulings.

Core Idea
Outward actions, not hidden beliefs, determine how we are treated in this world.

Maturidi, in his Kitab al-Tawhid, provides a scriptural proof to counter those who argue that inner faith alone matters. He cites three clear Quranic commands to fight disbelievers and polytheists, but notes that the fighting is based on what they manifest, not what they conceal. This passage establishes a key principle: in worldly affairs, we judge by the apparent, while the heart's true state is known only to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the repeated Quranic citations.
2
Identify the three Quranic verses
Find the three verses from Surah Tawbah that Maturidi quotes. They all command fighting against disbelievers or polytheists.
The verses are: 9:123, 9:36, and 9:5.
3
Understand the key observation
Maturidi points out that the fighting is based on what people manifest outwardly (shirk and kufr), not on what they conceal in their hearts.
This is the central point: outward action triggers the ruling.
4
Follow the logical inference
If outward shirk triggers fighting, then outward faith (verbal confession) should end it. Maturidi argues that this is exactly what the Quran shows.
The heart's true state remains hidden, but we act on the apparent.
5
Reflect on the implication
This passage supports the view that verbal confession is sufficient for legal purposes in this world, even though true faith resides in the heart.
Connect this to broader discussions of faith and works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم: قال الله عز وجل: ﴿قَاتِلُوا الَّذِينَ يَلُونَكُمْ مِنَ الْكُفَّارِ﴾ [التوبة: ١٢٣]، وقال: ﴿وَقَاتِلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ كَافَّةً﴾ [التوبة: ٣٦]، وقال: ﴿فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَيْثُ وَجَدْتُمُوهُمْ﴾ [التوبة: ٥]؛ ويقاتل على ما يظهرون من الشرك والكفر دون ما يضمرون، ولم يجب بهذا أن لا يكون الشرك والكفر بالقلوب. فما يبعد أن يُؤمر بالقتال حتى يؤمنوا، ثم يُمنَع القتال إذا أظهروا الإيمان باللسان وإن كان حقيقة موضع الإيمان القلب، إذ لا يمنع هذا كونه فيه. والله الموفق.
Then it is said to them: God Almighty said: 'Fight those who are adjacent to you of the disbelievers' [9:123], and He said: 'And fight the polytheists all together' [9:36], and He said: 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' [9:5]; and they are fought based on what they manifest of polytheism and disbelief, not what they conceal, and it does not follow from this that polytheism and disbelief are not in the hearts. So how far-fetched is it that he is commanded to fight until they believe, then fighting is prevented when they manifest faith by the tongue, even if the true locus of faith is the heart, since this does not prevent it from being in it. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof. Maturidi cites three Quranic verses that command fighting disbelievers and polytheists. He notes that the fighting is based on what they manifest outwardly, not on what they conceal. If fighting were based on inner disbelief, it would never stop because we cannot know hearts. But the Quran shows that when people outwardly profess faith, fighting ceases. Thus, outward profession is the basis for rulings, while inner faith remains in the heart. This supports the idea that verbal confession is a valid indicator.

Correction: Maturidi explicitly says fighting is based on outward manifestation, not inner concealment.

B) To show that fighting is based on outward manifestations

D) To argue against jihad

Key Takeaway
In this world, rulings are based on outward actions; the heart's true state is known only to Allah.

The Shahada: Legal Protection, Not Faith's Essence
Maturidi interprets the hadith on fighting until shahada to distinguish legal cause from faith reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi interprets the hadith on fighting until shahada to distinguish the legal function of testimony from the inner reality of faith.

Core Idea
The shahada spares life, but does not define the essence of faith.

Maturidi turns to a well-known prophetic hadith to reinforce his argument. This hadith is often cited to show that uttering the shahada is sufficient for worldly protection. But Maturidi draws a careful distinction: the shahada is a cause (sabab) for legal protection, not the inner reality (haqiqa) of faith. Understanding this distinction is key to his position on faith and actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice that the hadith mentions 'fighting until they say La ilaha illa Allah' and Maturidi's comment follows.
The Arabic is concise—reflect on its structure.
2
Identify the key claim
Maturidi says the two testimonies are a 'cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith.' What does this mean for the relationship between external utterance and inner belief?
3
Reflect on the distinction
Consider why this distinction matters for the broader debate about faith and works. If verbal confession only grants worldly security, what does it imply about the nature of faith?
This connects to Maturidi's view that faith is inner conviction (tasdiq), not mere utterance.
4
Connect to previous lessons
Recall earlier arguments about the definition of faith. This hadith supports the idea that the shahada suffices for legal rulings but does not define faith's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم في الخبر: أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله، وقيل: حتى يشهدوا، فيكون الشهادتان سبب منع القتل لا حقيقة الإيمان. والله الموفق.
Then it is said to them concerning the report: 'I was commanded to fight people until they say: There is no god but God', and it was said: 'until they testify', so the two testimonies are a cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This is another proof from a prophetic hadith. The hadith commands fighting until people utter the shahada. When they do, their lives are spared. Maturidi emphasizes that the shahada is a legal cause (sabab) for protection from killing, not the reality (haqiqa) of faith itself. This supports the argument that verbal confession is sufficient for worldly rulings (like protection of life) but does not define true faith.

Rational Proof: Faith Is Assent of the Heart
Maturidi argues rationally that faith is inner assent, not verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational argument that faith (iman) is fundamentally an inner assent of the heart, not merely verbal expression.

Core Idea
Faith is inner assent, not just words — because it can't be coerced and must exist where speech is forbidden.

Maturidi presents a rational proof that iman (faith) is not merely a verbal confession but an inner state of the heart. He begins with the linguistic meaning of iman as tasdiq (assent) and argues that the reality of faith is located in the heart because it cannot be coerced by external forces. He then strengthens his argument with a practical example: during prayer, one is forbidden to speak, yet faith is required, proving that faith is an inner reality independent of speech. This lesson unpacks his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall argument.
2
Understand the linguistic foundation
Notice that Maturidi starts with the linguistic definition of iman as tasdiq (assent) and its implication.
3
Follow the argument against coercion
Maturidi argues that faith cannot be coerced, so its locus is the heart, where no creature has authority.
4
Analyze the prayer example
Maturidi gives a concrete case: in prayer, one cannot verbally profess faith, yet faith is essential. If faith were verbal, prayer would invalidate faith.
5
Draw the conclusion
Conclude that faith must be an inner state of the heart, not merely outward speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما العقل فلأنه دين، والأديان تعقد، وما به اعتقادات الأديان القلوب، وكذلك. مع ما كان الإيمان في اللغة التصديق، وحقيقته الذي لا يُحتمل القهر والجبر هو الذي في القلب، إذ لا يجري فيه سلطان أحد من الخلق. وجملة ذلك أنه يجوز أن لا يكون لسان، ولا يُحتمل رفع الدين الحق ولا الإيمان بالله والرسل من أحد؛ ثبت أن حق ذلك القلب. مع ما كان ذلك من المحال ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحن في حال الخطاب بحال وباللسان؛ فعامة الأوقات على الخلق تمر بدونه؛ بل من الأحوال أحوال يُنهى المرء فيه أن يقول: آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك، نحو الكون في الصلاة، فيصير الإيمان على هذا القول بحيث ينهى، ودين الإسلام بحيث يُفسد عبادته؛ والله جعله شرطا للجواز.
As for the intellect, because [faith] is a religion, and religions are contracted, and that by which the beliefs of religions are [held] is the hearts. And likewise, since faith in language is tasdiq (assent), and its reality, which cannot be coerced, is that which is in the heart, for no one has authority over it. In sum, it is possible that there be no tongue, and it is not conceivable that true religion or faith in God and the messengers be removed from anyone; therefore it is established that the true locus of that is the heart. Moreover, it is absurd for the act of faith to be absent from the one tested in the situation of address by the tongue; for most times pass without it; rather, there are states in which one is forbidden to say 'I believe in the books and prophets and the resurrection' and the like, such as being in prayer. Then, according to this view, faith would become something that is prohibited, and the religion of Islam would become something that invalidates one's worship; yet God made it a condition for validity.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof. Maturidi argues from the linguistic meaning of iman as tasdiq (assent) that its reality is in the heart because it cannot be coerced by any creature. He then argues that if faith were merely verbal, it would be impossible to have faith in situations where speech is prohibited, such as during prayer. But prayer requires faith, so faith must be an inner state. Therefore, the true locus of faith is the heart, not the tongue.

Key Terms
عقل
دين
تصديق
قلب
لسان
صلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That verbal expression is always possible and therefore sufficient for faith.
Correction: Maturidi shows that verbal expression is not always possible (e.g., in prayer) and that faith is an inner assent that cannot be coerced, so it must be in the heart.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi say that faith cannot be merely verbal expression?
A) Because verbal expression is forbidden in prayer
B) Because the Quran says so
C) Because the Prophet said so
D) Because faith is a feeling

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates through reason that faith is an inner assent of the heart, not merely verbal confession, because it cannot be coerced and must remain valid even when speech is prohibited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you verbally declared something about your faith while your heart felt indifferent or doubtful? How does Maturidi's argument that faith is inner assent expose the gap between your words and your heart? What will you do to bring them into alignment starting today?
?
If you were placed in a situation where you could never speak about your faith again, would you be confident that your iman remains intact? What specific steps can you take now to strengthen the inner conviction of your heart so that it stands firm even when your tongue is silent?
?
This lesson teaches that faith cannot be coerced—no one can force genuine belief in your heart. Are there any areas in your life where you have been relying on external factors (e.g., routine, family pressure, social habit) to sustain your faith rather than a deep personal conviction? What would it cost you to replace that reliance with true inner tasdiq?

The Objection from Fighting Disbelievers and Maturidi's Reply
Maturidi answers the Karrami objection that outward fighting proves iman is verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that outward fighting against disbelievers targets their manifest shirk and kufr, not the inner reality of faith, and that verbal testimony is only a cause for protection, not the essence of iman.

Core Idea
Outward shirk is fought, not inner disbelief; confession protects life but does not equal faith.

The Karramiyya argued that because Muslims fight disbelievers until they confess, this shows iman is verbal. Maturidi responds by distinguishing between outward manifestation and inner reality, using Quranic verses and a key hadith to show that fighting is based on what is apparent, while faith resides in the heart. This lesson unpacks that critical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Maturidi's Quranic response
Read the Arabic passage carefully, focusing on how Maturidi cites three Quranic verses commanding fighting against disbelievers and polytheists. Notice that he emphasizes fighting is based on what they manifest.
The verses are from Surah at-Tawba.
2
Identify the distinction between outward and inward
Maturidi argues that fighting does not prove that shirk and kufr are not in the hearts. Instead, it proves that the command to fight is tied to outward actions. Reflect on how this answers the Karrami objection.
3
Analyze the hadith argument
Maturidi cites the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah' to show that the shahada is a cause for preventing killing, not the reality of faith. Compare this to the Quranic argument.
This reinforces that verbal confession does not define iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنه [هو] خاصة . فلم حُرموا به الغفران والموعود على الإيمان من النعيم الدائم والثواب / الجزيل ؟ ثم بما لا يجوز لهم عبادة في الحقيقة ولا ينالون بها فضيلة عند الله دليل على [١٩٥] أنهم ليسوا بمؤمنين. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يقال لهم : قال الله عز وجل: قاتلوا الذين يلونكم من الكفار ﴾ [ التوبة ، ۱۲۳/۹] . وقال وقاتلوا المشركين كافة ﴾ [التوبة، ٣٦/٩] وقال: ﴿فاقتلوا المشركين حيث وجدتموهم [ التوبة ، ٥/٩] ؛ ويقاتل على ما يظهرون من الشرك والكفر دون ما يضمرون، ولم ﴾ يجب بهذا أن لا يكون الشرك والكفر بالقلوب. فما يبعد أن يُؤمر بالقتال حتى يؤمنوا، ثم يُمنَع القتال إذا أظهروا الإيمان باللسان وإن كان حقيقة موضع الإيمان" القلب، إذ لا يمنع هذا کونه فيه . والله الموفق. ثم يقال لهم في الخبر أمرت أن أقاتل الناس حتى يقولوا لا إله إلا الله»، وقيل: «حتى يشهدوا ، فيكون الشهادتان سبب منع القتل لا حقيقة الإيمان. والله الموفق.
That [it] is specifically ... so why are they deprived through it of forgiveness and the promised eternal bliss and great reward for faith? Then because it is not permissible for them to worship in reality and they do not attain any virtue from Allah by it, this is proof that they are not believers. There is no power except with Allah. Then it is said to them: Allah Almighty said: 'Fight those who are adjacent to you of the disbelievers' [at-Tawba 123]. And He said: 'And fight the polytheists all together' [at-Tawba 36]. And He said: 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them' [at-Tawba 5]. And they are fought on account of what they manifest of shirk and kufr, not what they conceal, and this does not necessitate that shirk and kufr are not in the hearts. So what prevents that they are commanded to fight until they believe, then fighting is prevented when they manifest faith by the tongue even though the true place of faith is the heart? For this does not prevent that it [faith] is in it. And Allah is the Grantor of success. Then it is said to them concerning the hadith: 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say "There is no god but Allah,"' and it is said: 'until they bear witness,' so the two testimonies are a cause of preventing killing, not the reality of faith. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The Karramiyya argue that if iman is only in the heart, why are disbelievers deprived of forgiveness and fought? Maturidi replies that they are punished for outward shirk and kufr, not for hidden disbelief. He cites Quranic verses commanding fighting against disbelievers and polytheists, explaining that the fighting is based on what they manifest, not what they conceal. The command to fight continues until they show faith by the tongue, but this does not negate that true faith resides in the heart. He also cites the hadith 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say la ilaha illa Allah,' showing that the verbal testimony is a cause for protection from killing, not the reality of iman. Thus, outward confession does not define the essence of faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
كفر
شرك
لسان
قلب
شهادتان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Karramiyya believe that because Muslims fight disbelievers until they confess verbally, this proves that iman is purely verbal confession.
Correction: Maturidi shows that fighting is for outward shirk and kufr, and verbal confession is only a cause for protection, not the reality of faith.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of fighting disbelievers according to Maturidi's response?
A) To force them to have faith in the heart
B) To stop their outward shirk and kufr
C) To punish them for their inner disbelief
D) To make them utter the shahada only

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that fighting is based on manifest shirk, not inner disbelief, and that the shahada is a cause for protection, not the reality of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada, do you ever stop to examine whether your heart truly affirms it, or do you rely on the words alone to feel secure? What would you do if you found your heart was not fully attuned?
?
How often do you judge others' faith based on their outward actions—like prayers or attendance—while ignoring the state of your own inner conviction? In light of Maturidi's argument, what accountability does that place on you?
?
If your life were threatened for your faith, would your tongue confess while your heart trembled? Are you willing to ask Allah to purify your heart so that your words and inner reality are one?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
8 min
Maturidi's Rational Proof that Faith is in the Heart
Maturidi argues rationally that iman is inner affirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational arguments for why true faith (iman) must be inner affirmation (tasdiq) in the heart, not merely verbal confession.

Core Idea
Faith is inner affirmation; the tongue can be coerced but the heart cannot.

Maturidi offers several rational proofs to show that iman is fundamentally a matter of the heart. He begins with the linguistic meaning of iman as tasdiq, then argues that what can be coerced cannot be true faith, and that there are situations where verbal confession is prohibited. This lesson unpacks his arguments and shows why the Karramiyya view is mistaken.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the flow of Maturidi's argument sink in before dissecting it.
Notice how Maturidi uses multiple rational proofs in sequence.
2
Identify the linguistic and rational basis
Maturidi starts by stating that iman is a religion and religions are held in hearts. Then he notes that linguistically iman means tasdiq, and its essence is what cannot be coerced. Find these points in the text.
The linguistic definition is key to his argument.
3
Examine the arguments from coercion and possibility
Maturidi argues that what can be coerced cannot be true faith, and that a person can exist without a tongue but not without faith in the heart. Reflect on why these points are rational proofs.
Coercion is impossible on the heart.
4
Consider the prayer argument
Maturidi points out that during prayer, one is prohibited from saying certain words of faith. If faith were verbal, prayer would prohibit faith, which is absurd. This refutes the Karramiyya.
This is a powerful reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما العقل فلأنه دين، والأديان تعقد ، وما به اعتقادات الأديان القلوب، وكذلك . مع ما كان الإيمان في اللغة التصديق، وحقيقته الذي لا يُحتمل القهر والجبر هو الذي في القلب، إذ لا يجري [فيه] سلطان أحد من الخلق. وجملة ذلك أنه يجوز أن لا يكون لسان، ولا يُحتمل رفع الدين الحق ولا الإيمان بالله والرسل من أحد؛ ثبت أن حق ذلك القلب. مع ما كان ذلك من المحال ارتفاع فعل الإيمان عن الممتحن في حال الخطاب بحال وباللسان؛ [ف] عامة الأوقات على الخلق تمر بدونه ؛ بل من الأحوال أحوال يُنهى المرء فيه أن يقول : آمنت بالكتب والنبيين والبعث ونحو ذلك، نحو الكون في الصلاة"، فيصير الإيمان على هذا القول بحيث ينهى، ودين الإسلام بحيث يُفسد عبادته ؛ والله جعله شرطا للجواز "، وجعله دائما لا يتغير ولا يتبدل ولا يجوز فيه النسخ . ثبت أنه على غير ما ظنت الكرامية . على [۱۹۰] أن الله تعالى أعلى درجة / الإيمان في القلوب حتى صيّرها أعلى الدرجات، وصيّر الإيمان مما يقوم به الخيرات، وعند وجوده يصلح العبادات ؛ وما يحتمل ما وصفت إنما هو القلوب لا الألسن، لذلك كانت أحق .
And as for the intellect, because it is a religion, and religions are held, and that by which the beliefs of religions are [held] is the hearts, and likewise. Since faith linguistically is tasdiq, and its reality which cannot be coerced or compelled is that which is in the heart, for no created being has authority over it. The sum of that is that it is possible that there be no tongue, and it is not permissible to remove the true religion nor faith in Allah and His messengers from anyone; so it is established that the reality of that is the heart. Moreover, it is impossible that the act of faith be absent from the tested person at the time of address by state and by tongue; [for] most times pass over creation without it [the tongue]; rather, among the states are states in which a person is prohibited from saying, 'I believe in the books, prophets, resurrection,' and the like, such as being in prayer. So according to this view, faith would be something that is prohibited, and the religion of Islam would be something that corrupts one's worship. And Allah made it a condition for validity, and made it perpetual, not changing, not altering, and not subject to abrogation. It is established that it is contrary to what the Karramiyya thought. Indeed, Allah Almighty made the degree of faith higher in the hearts, making them the highest degrees, and made faith something by which good deeds are performed, and upon its existence acts of worship are valid. And that which can bear what I have described is only the hearts, not the tongues. Therefore they are more deserving.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a rational argument. Maturidi begins by stating that iman is a religion, and religions are held in the hearts. Linguistically, iman means tasdiq (affirmation), and its reality is that which cannot be subjected to coercion or compulsion; this is what is in the heart, because no created being has authority over it. He argues that a person can exist without a tongue, but cannot be divested of the true religion or faith in Allah and His messengers from one's heart. Moreover, it is impossible for the act of faith to be absent from the tested person at the time of divine address, since most times people go through life without verbal expression. In fact, there are situations where a person is prohibited from saying 'I believe in the books, prophets, resurrection,' such as during prayer. If iman were verbal, then performing prayer would involve a prohibition of iman, which would corrupt worship. But Allah has made iman a condition for the validity of worship and made it perpetual and unchangeable. This is contrary to the Karramiyya view. Finally, Allah has placed iman in the hearts, making it the highest degree, and only hearts can bear the qualities described, not tongues.

Key Terms
تصديق
قلب
لسان
كرامية
إكراه
صلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That iman is merely verbal confession.
Correction: Maturidi shows that iman is essentially inner affirmation (tasdiq) because it cannot be coerced and there are situations where verbal confession is prohibited, such as during prayer.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that iman cannot be merely verbal?
A) Because the tongue can be coerced
B) Because it is impossible to always speak
C) Because there are situations where speaking faith is prohibited
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
True faith (iman) is the heart's affirmation, not just verbal confession, as it alone is immune to coercion and consistent with Islamic practice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I believe' with your tongue, do you ever feel a disconnect from what your heart truly holds? What is one area where your heart's affirmation does not match your words, and what will you do about it today?
?
This lesson teaches that true faith is secure in the heart and cannot be removed by any external force. Is your heart's faith strong enough that if you were forced to deny it verbally, you would remain firm? What can you do to strengthen that inner conviction starting this week?
?
The example of prayer shows that even worship can be corrupted if we prioritize speech over heart. In your own prayer, do you focus more on the words or on the inner presence of faith? What specific change will you make from your next prayer to ensure your heart is fully present?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate

Quranic Evidence that Iman is in the Heart
Maturidi uses Quranic verses to prove iman is in the heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses to prove that the reality of faith resides in the heart, not the tongue.

Core Idea
Faith is in the heart because the tongue can be forced, but Allah forbids compulsion.

Maturidi presents a series of Quranic arguments to establish that iman is fundamentally an inner reality of the heart, not merely a verbal declaration. The passage begins by noting that faith is known through thought and reflection, which are heart-acts, then cites the verse 'No compulsion in religion' to exclude the tongue, and finally uses the Quran's own address to believers as evidence. Let's unpack these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then the translation. Notice how Maturidi moves from one Quranic evidence to the next.
The passage is dense; multiple proofs are packed together.
2
Understand the first argument: faith known by thought and reflection
Maturidi states that the reality of faith is known through 'thought and reflection' (fikr and nazar), which are works of the heart. This sets the stage that faith is an inner act.
This is a foundational premise: iman is linked to intellectual acts of the heart.
3
Analyze the 'no compulsion' argument
The verse 'No compulsion in religion' is used to argue that faith cannot be in the tongue because the tongue can be coerced. If faith were merely verbal, it could be forced, contradicting the Quranic principle.
This is a key point: the tongue is like other instruments that can be compelled.
4
Examine the evidence from Quranic address
Maturidi notes that the Quran addresses believers as 'O you who believe' even when they are not uttering faith verbally. This shows that the reality of faith exists in them at that moment, which can only be in the heart.
The address includes all who have iman, regardless of current speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فإن الخطاب بالإيمان يلزم بالعقول، ويُعرف حقيقة ما به الإيمان بالفكر والنظر وذلك عمل القلوب، فمثله الإيمان. مع ما كان الألسن قد تستعمل وتجبر كغيرها من الآلات ، والله تعالى يقول : لا إكراه في الدين ﴾ [البقرة، ٢٥٦/٢] ، فلم يجز أن يجعل حقيقته فيما فيه الإكراه. وقال الله تعالى: فمن يكفر بالطاغوت ويؤمن بالله ﴾ [البقرة، ٢٥٦/٢] وليس الكفر بالطاغوت باللسان خاصة، فمثله الإيمان ألا يُرى إلى قوله : ألم تر إلى الذين يزعمون إلى قوله : وقد أمروا أن يكفروا به ، فيصير الميل والتحاكم ترك للإيمان وإن أخبر عن لسانه أنه يزعم أنه مؤمن بالذي عليه الإيمان به والله الموفق. و في كتاب الله الخطاب بقوله : يا أيها الذين آمنوا في غير موضع " ، ثم لم يرتب أحد ممن ينسب إلى الإسلام والإيمان في ذلك أنه من تضمنه، وإن لم يكن هو وقت فرع الخطاب معه يستعمل لسانه في فعل الإيمان ثبت أن حقيقته التي بها سمّاهم بهذا قائمة فيهم وقت الخطاب، وهي لا تحتمل إلا أن تكون في القلب ولا قوة إلا بالله
Moreover, the address of faith is binding upon the intellects, and the reality of that by which faith [is] is known through thought and reflection, and that is the work of the hearts. So faith is similar. And since tongues may be used and coerced like other instruments, and Allah Almighty says: 'There is no compulsion in religion' [al-Baqara 256], it is not permissible to make its reality in that which involves compulsion. And Allah Almighty said: 'So whoever disbelieves in the taghut and believes in Allah' [al-Baqara 256], and disbelief in the taghut is not specifically by the tongue, so faith is similar. Do you not see His saying: 'Have you not seen those who claim' until His saying: 'and they have been commanded to disbelieve in it' [an-Nisa 60]? Thus inclination and arbitration become abandonment of faith even if he reports from his tongue that he claims to be a believer in that which he should have faith in. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And in the Book of Allah, the address 'O you who believe' occurs in numerous places, and no one who attributes himself to Islam and faith has doubted that it includes them, even if at the time of the address he is not using his tongue for the act of faith. So it is established that the reality by which He named them with this is existing in them at the time of the address, and it cannot be except in the heart. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage presents Quranic evidence. Maturidi first states that the address to faith is binding on the intellect, and the reality of faith is known through thought and reflection, which are works of the heart. Therefore, faith is akin to that. He then points out that tongues can be forced, but Allah says 'There is no compulsion in religion' (Quran 2:256), so it is not permissible to place the reality of faith in something that involves compulsion. He also cites the verse 'So whoever disbelieves in the taghut and believes in Allah' (Quran 2:256) and notes that disbelief in the taghut is not specifically by the tongue. Then he refers to the verse about those who claim faith but seek judgment from taghut (Quran 4:60), showing that inclining to taghut is abandonment of faith, even if the tongue claims otherwise. Finally, he notes that the Quran addresses believers as 'O you who believe' many times, and no one doubts that it includes them, even if at that moment they are not uttering the words of faith. This proves that the reality by which they are called believers is existing in them at the time of address, and it can only be in the heart.

Key Terms
لا إكراه في الدين
يا أيها الذين آمنوا
طاغوت
فكر
نظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Quranic address 'O you who believe' implies they are verbally professing at that moment.
Correction: Maturidi shows the address includes them even when not speaking, proving the reality of faith is in the heart.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic principle does Maturidi use to argue that iman cannot be in the tongue?
A) 'Kill the polytheists wherever you find them'
B) 'There is no compulsion in religion'
C) 'Fight those who are adjacent to you'
D) 'Have you not seen those who claim'

Key Takeaway
The reality of faith is in the heart; the tongue is only an instrument that can be coerced, but true faith is a matter of inner conviction.
